  //<![CDATA[
    function loadScript(url, callback) {
      var script = document.createElement("script");
      script.type = "text/javascript";
    
      if (script.readyState) {  //Internet Explorer
          script.onreadystatechange = function() {
            if (script.readyState == "loaded" ||
                    script.readyState == "complete") {
              script.onreadystatechange = null;
              callback();
            }
          };
      } else {  //Other browsers
        script.onload = function() {
          callback();
        };
      }
    
      script.src = url;
      document.getElementsByTagName("head")[0].appendChild(script);
    }
    
    function initAppleId() {
      AppleID.auth.init({
        clientId : 'com.goodreads.app', 
        scope : 'name email',
        redirectURI: 'https://www.goodreads.com/apple_users/sign_in_with_apple_web',
        state: 'apple_oauth_state_98f9d148-b3c5-4fdd-b05c-2ad43a10b5e8'
      });
    }
    
    var initializeSiwa = function() {
      var APPLE_SIGN_IN_JS_URL =  "https://appleid.cdn-apple.com/appleauth/static/jsapi/appleid/1/en_US/appleid.auth.js"
      loadScript(APPLE_SIGN_IN_JS_URL, initAppleId);
    };

      initializeSiwa();

  <span id="freeText13218399803255135261" style="display:none">De jonge Tiuri verbreekt de regels, die bepalen dat hij met niemand mag praten in de nacht voordat hij tot ridder zal worden geslagen. <div class='answererUserIcon'>
<a class="leftAlignedImage userPhoto" href="/user/show/4428808-paulina-sanchez"><img alt="" src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/users/1414389324i/4428808._UX100_CR0,0,100,100_.jpg" /></a>

<span class='communityAnswererName'>

<span class='communityAnswerText'>
<span class="expandableContainer"><span class="truncatedContent">No! There are many many differences. The main one being that there's zero magic or supernatural powers in the book. Also, the characters are very diff<a class="jsShow showAction" href="#">…more</a></span><span class="fullContent">No! There are many many differences. The main one being that there's zero magic or supernatural powers in the book. Also, the characters are very different since the book focuses only on Tiuri and his journey. We do get context from other characters he meets along the way but it's all from his point of view. I personally loved the book more than the Netflix series.<a class="jsHide hideAction" href="#">(less)</a></span></span>
</span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback 9781782690269" href="/book/show/21028440-the-letter-for-the-king">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5157918-jv-poore?shelf=middle-grade">middle-grade</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5157918-jv-poore?shelf=mystery">mystery</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5157918-jv-poore?shelf=survival-stories">survival-stories</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5157918-jv-poore?shelf=own-it-arc">own-it-arc</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5157918-jv-poore?shelf=buried-under-books">buried-under-books</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5157918-jv-poore?shelf=legends-myths-fables">legends-myths-fables</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1568812836" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer7303519445646029551">Upon discovering a character I admire and adore, I often aspire to become that character. Emulate a new role model, envision greater goals and dream of different worlds to conquer. In this case, though, I would never set myself up for that fall. Merely a human being, a perfectly plausible person; Tiuri is genuinely good. And kind. I believe that Tiuri is truly and actually, altruistic.<br/><br/>His epic journey to deliver a message of monumental importance took place many years ago. A mission that today c</span>
  <span id="freeText7303519445646029551" style="display:none">Upon discovering a character I admire and adore, I often aspire to become that character. Emulate a new role model, envision greater goals and dream of different worlds to conquer. In this case, though, I would never set myself up for that fall. Merely a human being, a perfectly plausible person; Tiuri is genuinely good. And kind. I believe that Tiuri is truly and actually, altruistic.<br /><br />His epic journey to deliver a message of monumental importance took place many years ago. A mission that today could be as simple as “send”, was an adventure only for the courageous and strong then. Traveling alone, on horseback at best; stumbling through the forest by sheer will, hiding from the knights who considered him a murderer and a thief, at worst.<br /><br />Tiuri is brave. No. Make that, bold—often foolishly so. Although, to be fair, no fault can ever be found. If ever there was a quintessential example of will power (aside from Frog &amp; Toad “Cookies”, that is), Tiuri conveys it. Wise beyond his years he is also, oddly, naïve. A sincere listener, Tiuri ponders then proceeds. Complexly concurrent, he has an uncanny ability to act instinctively. <br /><br />But I’ve buried the lead. <br /><br />Tiuri should not even be embarking on this endeavor. Moments before he fled his kingdom, fleet on a stolen horse, with the furious owner following; Tiuri had been locked inside a silent chapel, reflecting upon the duties he would perform as knight to his beloved king; beginning at sunrise.<br /><br />Tiuri’s abrupt departure meant sacrificing what he had worked towards his whole life (all sixteen years of it). His decision seems reckless and a bit ridiculous. But things aren’t always as they seem, and this cunning theme cuts through narrative cleverly guiding Tiuri as he encounters a plethora of peculiar people during his travels. <br /><br />The Letter for the King reads like an instant classic. While the fiction is fresh, the feel is familiar. Mystery and intrigue magnificently merge with action and adventure, appealing to all senses. The colorful characters encountered keep loneliness at bay and Tiuri on his toes. 11-year-old-me would have read this book over and over and over.<br /><br />This review was written for Buried Under Books by jv poore.</span>
  <a data-text-id="7303519445646029551" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_2329334110" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2329334110" />
    <a title="Sara" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/1170391-sara"><img alt="Sara" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1590218363p2/1170391.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2329334110?book_show_action=true">Apr 04, 2019</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Sara" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Sara" href="/user/show/1170391-sara">Sara</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback 9781782690818" href="/book/show/23633448-the-letter-for-the-king">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1170391-sara?shelf=fiction">fiction</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1170391-sara?shelf=young-adult">young-adult</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1170391-sara?shelf=arc">arc</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1170391-sara?shelf=fantasy">fantasy</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2329334110" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer14374718666858513608">I received a copy of this book in exchange for an honest review.<br/><br/>It’s been a long time since I’ve read a story that manages to capture the spirit and emotions of an epic adventure, but The Letter For the King manages to do just that. It’s full of secrets, missions from strangers, and the feeling that you can accomplish anything, be anything, that you want to.<br/><br/>Tiuri is about to become a knight when he’s given a task by a stranger. He must deliver a letter to the king. And on his way to do this, he </span>
  <span id="freeText14374718666858513608" style="display:none">I received a copy of this book in exchange for an honest review.<br /><br />It’s been a long time since I’ve read a story that manages to capture the spirit and emotions of an epic adventure, but The Letter For the King manages to do just that. It’s full of secrets, missions from strangers, and the feeling that you can accomplish anything, be anything, that you want to.<br /><br />Tiuri is about to become a knight when he’s given a task by a stranger. He must deliver a letter to the king. And on his way to do this, he meets a wonderful and colourful cast of people - good and evil, who will help or hinder his mission. <br /><br />It’s a very traditional fantasy tale, that encompasses a long journey and a naive and pure hero at the heart of it. The writing is simple, without any nuances or subtleties to the text, and the story itself follows a pattern that’s often repeated (good guy meets another guy at the right time and place, repeat), but it’s the message behind it that struck me more than anything else. It’s wholesome and light and welcoming. It feels homey and nice. There’s definitely a hint of the nostalgia about it that I miss in more modern fantasy stories. Tiuri is developed enough that you care about his quest and want him to succeed. He’s the very definition of ‘pure at heart’ and his emotional development, and strong friendship with guide Piak, is nice to see unfold. <br /><br /><br />It’s not going to appeal to everyone, as the plot is simplistic, but fans of ‘old fashioned’ fantasy should give this a go.</span>
  <a data-text-id="14374718666858513608" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<span id="freeTextContainer7063521414296807735">Oh, give me a sec to let my tears drop. <br/><br/>This book is beautiful. The story inside feels so real. It feels different. It almost feels like Tiuri, the main character here, sits across the room telling me the story himself, and help me learnt so much.<br/>I won't forget this book, that is for sure.<br/>I am glad I found this book in my school library a few days ago.   <span id="freeText7063521414296807735" style="display:none">Oh, give me a sec to let my tears drop. <br /><br />This book is beautiful. The story inside feels so real. It feels different. It almost feels like Tiuri, the main character here, sits across the room telling me the story himself, and help me learnt so much.<br />I won't forget this book, that is for sure.<br />I am glad I found this book in my school library a few days ago. This is beyond my imagination.<br />I had no expectation when I first saw this book. I thought to myself that maybe this is another freakish classic tale, written with so much art and deep thoughts and evil mixed in. But what I found is surprising.<br /><br />After a few pages I realized how this book feels so pure and unreal but real at the same time. How this book did nothing but touching its readers and send them great values of life that they learn by themself. <br /><br />It is a book for kids.. but it is an awesome book. Oh let me cry for a little bit more, for this book is beautiful.<br />I ridiculously love it, I learnt so much from it, gosh I just adore it. <br /><br />It doesn't feel old or boring. It's awesome.<br />The characters are all males most of the time, guys that shared the same age with me right now. <br /><br />The story is about a journey of Tiuri, a young man that ran away on the night before he could be the king's knight, for a secret mission given by strangers. On his journey he met a lot of people, become friends with so many people, and face so much danger. The story tells about how he discovered a lot of things about life, about himself, about the world.<br /><br />Some sentences here punch in a huge impression in my heart, like the time when Tiuri finished his mission and a wise clown from the neighbour country told him a story of a guy who went on a journey to chase the end of the rainbow, for he believed that the end of the rainbow would be the most beautiful place on earth. However l, after the long trip he found nothing. He was disappointed, but then he thought about the journey he had, how he met so many awesome new friends, beautiful sights,and a lot of happiness, he realized that the rainbow is not the most important thing! Thee beauty and values he found in his journey, that is the most important. <br /><br />This book is crazily awesome, I hope my son or daughter will read it one day and feel the same thing.<br />This book gave me a lot. One of the most inspiring book ever. :) I also hope you'll consider reading it too, even thou the cover of it might not look that interesting, haha. Happy reading, and God bless your journey :")</span>

<span id="freeTextContainer17243325945387225292">3.5 stars from me<br/>4.75 stars from my son<br/><br/>I read this with my 10 year old son for the kids bookclub he belongs to through one of our local independent bookstores. It wasn't one I had previously heard of, although it is a Dutch classic, where it was originally published in 1962.<br/><br/>This is quaintly written old fashioned chivalric fantasy which would provide a nice entry to the genre for middle grade and young adult audiences.   <span id="freeText17243325945387225292" style="display:none">3.5 stars from me<br />4.75 stars from my son<br /><br />I read this with my 10 year old son for the kids bookclub he belongs to through one of our local independent bookstores. It wasn't one I had previously heard of, although it is a Dutch classic, where it was originally published in 1962.<br /><br />This is quaintly written old fashioned chivalric fantasy which would provide a nice entry to the genre for middle grade and young adult audiences. It's an older book, and reads that way, but it nevertheless has a simple appeal that keeps it fresh enough for modern readers.<br /><br />My son is not new to fantasy, and he quite enjoyed this. Aside from the story, he loved the included map and black and white illustrations done by the author. It was quite an accomplishment for him to tackle a book that comes in at just over 500 pages, but the story moves along at a nice pace that ended up making the length less daunting for him.<br /><br /></span>

<span id="freeTextContainer14337115852800107828">As YA goes, this is a 5-star plot. It was written in 1962, apparently, and the new translation is coming on 25 August of 2015.<br/><br/>It's the story of a squire on the eve of becoming a knight who does NOT become a knight because he makes the fateful decision to answer a call for help. One thing leads to another, and before long, this kid is on a quest with unseen enemies all around him (but with unexpected friends as well).<br/><br/>It's sweet, actually. So old school it will remind you of the type of book about</span>
  <span id="freeText14337115852800107828" style="display:none">As YA goes, this is a 5-star plot. It was written in 1962, apparently, and the new translation is coming on 25 August of 2015.<br /><br />It's the story of a squire on the eve of becoming a knight who does NOT become a knight because he makes the fateful decision to answer a call for help. One thing leads to another, and before long, this kid is on a quest with unseen enemies all around him (but with unexpected friends as well).<br /><br />It's sweet, actually. So old school it will remind you of the type of book about knighthood you could not put down as a kid. A simpler world of good and evil, don't you know. An antidote to the gray confusions in our time.<br /><br />Memory Lane, anyone? I suspect reluctant readers and fans of all things medieval will love it. </span>

<div id="review_2513867731" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2513867731" />
    <a title="The Captain" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/54489623-the-captain"><img alt="The Captain" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1459976325p2/54489623.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2513867731?book_show_action=true">Aug 31, 2018</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="The Captain" class="user" itemprop="url" name="The Captain" href="/user/show/54489623-the-captain">The Captain</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="did not like it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">did not like it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback 9781782690818" href="/book/show/23633448-the-letter-for-the-king">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/54489623-the-captain?shelf=young-adult">young-adult</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2513867731" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer10972184867568041776">Ahoy there me mateys!  I received this young adult fantasy eARC from NetGalley in exchange for an honest review.  So here be me honest musings . . .<br/><br/>I always be interested in fairy tales from other lands.  This translation caught me eye because the author was born in Indonesia, imprisoned in a Japanese internment camp in WWII, and then moved to the Netherlands.  She published this book in 1962 and it won the Children's Book of the Year Award and was subsequently translated into sixteen languages.</span>
  <span id="freeText10972184867568041776" style="display:none">Ahoy there me mateys!  I received this young adult fantasy eARC from NetGalley in exchange for an honest review.  So here be me honest musings . . .<br /><br />I always be interested in fairy tales from other lands.  This translation caught me eye because the author was born in Indonesia, imprisoned in a Japanese internment camp in WWII, and then moved to the Netherlands.  She published this book in 1962 and it won the Children's Book of the Year Award and was subsequently translated into sixteen languages.  Apparently it is also becoming a Netflix series.  So I had to know what the hype was about.<br /><br />And sadly I have to say that I don't really get it.  The story follows a boy named Tiuri.  He was standing vigil on the night before becoming a Knight when he chooses to leave the chapel in order to deliver an urgent message.  What was supposed to be a simple task instead becomes a quest to deliver a message to a king in another land.<br /><br />This book is a fairly straightforward and simplistic tale where the young squire is always meeting people at just the right time to help him and nothing bad really ever happens.  Tiuri is supposed to be 16 but comes across as being much younger.  His naivete seemed to make him more like ten or so.  He is honorable and makes friends wherever he goes.<br /><br />Unfortunately there was no real tension and I was pretty disconnected from the story.  It was a quick read even though the time dragged when actually reading it.   The world building wasn't that exciting either.  With slow pacing and not much action, I was tempted to not finish this one.  I did finish it but didn't really like it and will not reread it.  I wish it had been better.<br /><br />So lastly . . .<br /><br />Thank you Pushkin Children's Books!<br /><br />Check out me other reviews at <a target="_blank" rel="noopener nofollow" href="https://thecaptainsquartersblog.wordpress.com/">https://thecaptainsquartersblog.wordp...</a></span>
  <a data-text-id="10972184867568041776" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_1531429563" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1531429563" />
    <a title="Hannah" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/10781987-hannah"><img alt="Hannah" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1546636818p2/10781987.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1531429563?book_show_action=true">Jan 30, 2016</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Hannah" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Hannah" href="/user/show/10781987-hannah">Hannah</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was ok"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was ok</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Hardcover 9780545819787" href="/book/show/24612565-the-letter-for-the-king">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/10781987-hannah?shelf=around-the-world-in-80-books">around-the-world-in-80-books</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/10781987-hannah?shelf=mg">mg</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/10781987-hannah?shelf=fantasy">fantasy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/10781987-hannah?shelf=ya">ya</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1531429563" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer17562655776825173679">This is a prime example of a book that needs an introduction. The original Dutch edition of <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/21028440.The_Letter_for_the_King' title='The Letter for the King by Tonke Dragt' rel='nofollow noopener'>The Letter for the King</a> was published in 1962 by an Indonesian survivor of WWII Japanese internment camps and is considered to be a European children's classic. 50 years later, it was finally translated into English.<br/><br/>So how does it hold up? Poorly, when you consider how the English edition was marketed. <br/><br/>I found it on a YA shelf with a shiny cover promising the epic adventures of a 16-year old squire. Sound</span>
  <span id="freeText17562655776825173679" style="display:none">This is a prime example of a book that needs an introduction. The original Dutch edition of <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/21028440.The_Letter_for_the_King" title="The Letter for the King by Tonke Dragt" rel="nofollow noopener">The Letter for the King</a> was published in 1962 by an Indonesian survivor of WWII Japanese internment camps and is considered to be a European children's classic. 50 years later, it was finally translated into English.<br /><br />So how does it hold up? Poorly, when you consider how the English edition was marketed. <br /><br />I found it on a YA shelf with a shiny cover promising the epic adventures of a 16-year old squire. Sounds like YA, right? What was inside was an intensely linear plot with zero moral complexity, character development, or twists. The villains are uniformly murderous and come from <i>Evilland</i> (Eviellan), women exist solely to feed Tiuri (though one gives him some chain mail), and there's never a difficult decision - not even a wrong turn on a road. The writing does absolutely nothing for me, though that's hard to judge from a translation.<br /><br />Had I been faced with an edition that started with a formal introduction to <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/148470.Tonke_Dragt" title="Tonke Dragt" rel="nofollow noopener">Tonke Dragt</a> (who seems very interesting) and the history of Dutch children's lit, I would have had a better frame of reference for reading and perhaps enjoying the book. However, given the way this printing was presented, I would advise readers after a children's medieval adventure to pick up more recent MG books like <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/60400.The_Ruins_of_Gorlan__Ranger_s_Apprentice___1_" title="The Ruins of Gorlan (Ranger's Apprentice, #1) by John Flanagan" rel="nofollow noopener">The Ruins of Gorlan</a> or <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/153784.First_Test__Protector_of_the_Small___1_" title="First Test (Protector of the Small, #1) by Tamora Pierce" rel="nofollow noopener">First Test</a> instead. They're still fairly straightforward, but at least there's <i>something</i> going on in terms of plot and character.<br /><br />If you are an adult determined to read the translation, save it for reading aloud to kids under 10.</span>
  <a data-text-id="17562655776825173679" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_1413929847" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1413929847" />
    <a title="Mathew" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/42270985-mathew"><img alt="Mathew" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1554409562p2/42270985.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1413929847?book_show_action=true">Oct 11, 2015</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Mathew" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Mathew" href="/user/show/42270985-mathew">Mathew</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback 9781782690269" href="/book/show/21028440-the-letter-for-the-king">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/42270985-mathew?shelf=being-yourself">being-yourself</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/42270985-mathew?shelf=childrens-literature">childrens-literature</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/42270985-mathew?shelf=disguised-identity">disguised-identity</a>,

              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/42270985-mathew?shelf=kindness">kindness</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/42270985-mathew?shelf=quest">quest</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/42270985-mathew?shelf=identity">identity</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/42270985-mathew?shelf=key-stage-2">key-stage-2</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/42270985-mathew?shelf=family">family</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/42270985-mathew?shelf=friendship">friendship</a>
          </div>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1413929847" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer8800251914934745365">First released 50 odd years ago in the Netherlands, this is a wonderful story of knights and adventures written by Tonke Dragt: why it took so long to be spotted over here (it's sold over a million copies) and be translated is beyond me. <br/>From the outset, when Tiuri is tempted from his night's vigil out of the chapel by a call for help, I was hooked. There was something about Tiuri, the use of limited third person (wonderfully translated by Laura Watkinson) and the style of narrative that reminde</span>
  <span id="freeText8800251914934745365" style="display:none">First released 50 odd years ago in the Netherlands, this is a wonderful story of knights and adventures written by Tonke Dragt: why it took so long to be spotted over here (it's sold over a million copies) and be translated is beyond me. <br />From the outset, when Tiuri is tempted from his night's vigil out of the chapel by a call for help, I was hooked. There was something about Tiuri, the use of limited third person (wonderfully translated by Laura Watkinson) and the style of narrative that reminded me of the first Harry Potter book. Whether it was this idea that the world felt very real from the start or that there was something in Tiuri's character was drew me in as much as Harry did, I don't know but I knew that I couldn't stop thinking about the story when I wasn't reading it. I wanted to know what happened next and I cared for Tiuri and his good friend Piak. <br /><br />The story takes place within two neighbouring kingdoms who have been at peace since as long as anyone can remember but there are whispers are a growing army to the south who threaten to destroy that the people of Dagonaut and Unauwen hold dear. It is up to Tiuri to carry an important letter to the king of west about this impending danger but on the way, spies and evil knights will not stop at anything to take this letter from Tiuri even if it means his death. <br />A pleasant surprise for me in this book was the little amount of battle and death. You would think with all the swords and horses trampling around that it would be common yet Tiuri's encounters are almost like reading Bunyan's The Pilgrim's Progress. It is not his ability to wield a sword that saves him but rather his mind and his heart against the challenges ahead. This book is a hefty 508 pages long but the chapters are short and snappy and I found the pace to be as quick as Tiuri's own horse. Although there is a lack of strong female characters, I would consider this as a whole class read for UKS2 because the sense of chase throughout is quite gripping. <br /><br />Cross-Curricular Suggestions:Year 5<br />English:<br />I would certain make use of the thematic links that are prevalent and have similar books available as well as classic books involving knights (King Arthur) in my reading corner through my time reading this book to the class. <br />I like the idea of the children creating their own knight who is loyal to one of the good kings and who is sent on their own quest to find out about the red riders. I think children would enjoy creating either their male of female knight, working on character description but then planning and writing an extended narrative much in the same style as the King Arthur stories. <br /><br />Maths:<br />As soon as I saw the fractions expectations, I did think that designing their own knight's shield could lead to some fractions work where they section off different parts of the shield in terms of the fraction that they are studying and they could then illustrate it. Certainly counting up the perimeter and area of different places that Tiuri visits on his journey could be interesting as well as measuring angles of photos of castles would also support using the book in context. Finally, because the book is so huge, there is ample scope for word problems involving all elements of the Maths skills the children are expected to cover. <br /><br />History: <br />I think there is a lot of scope for exploring British history from an Anglo-saxon perspective considering King Arthur was meant to be around that time too. Looking at weaponry as well as clothing and a sense of time and place according to landscape (natural and human) could really help bring the text to life as well as make the topic a little more exciting. <br /><br />Art: <br />I really like the idea of using wooden mannequins to try and get the children to play with the human form and consider poses the Tiuri could be in throughout the book. They would have to consider and sketch the different types of clothing that he wore throughout and play with texture and tone. They could also, if you wanted to take a really exciting and challenging approach, have a go at some sculpture alongside sketching and try to make their own Ardanwen (Tiuri's magnificent horse)out of clay.<br /><br />DT: <br />I quite like the idea of them creating their own castle from junk modelling (sketching and planning first) but with having in it a working circuit to indicate lights going on in towers (simple circuits) and also a switch approaches that raises and lowers the drawbridge. <br /><br />Music: <br />I would offer the opportunity for the children to use instruments to create some music based on instruments using during the Anglo-Saxon period and onwards (the Dark Ages). The focus would be to make some courtly music that Tiuri might here in the different castles. Children could dress up and play their piece to the assembly and the music could tell the story of a famous deed of one of the knights (no singing required!)<br /><br /> </span>
  <a data-text-id="8800251914934745365" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<span id="freeTextContainer2727068881856790632">My father has always faintly disliked reading. Too bad he got me as a daughter! Out of the countless of books that he read to me when I was small, this book and its sequel are by far the most memorable. It fed my imagination to no ends, spawning both great visions and one of the most terrifying nightmares I remember. Since back then, much has changed.   <span id="freeText2727068881856790632" style="display:none">My father has always faintly disliked reading. Too bad he got me as a daughter! Out of the countless of books that he read to me when I was small, this book and its sequel are by far the most memorable. It fed my imagination to no ends, spawning both great visions and one of the most terrifying nightmares I remember. Since back then, much has changed. My knowledge of the Dutch language might have become crippled, and my eyes feast on the pages of other fantasy masterpieces, but Tonke Dragt and this book has always a place amongst my favourites. I'd also go as far as to claim, that as an aspiring fantasy writer, this book has been one of the many little influences that set me on this path.<br /><i>De brief voor de koning</i> was a glorious experience to me many years ago, and will no doubt offer the same delight to any other child fond of books today.</span>

    <div class="section">
      

<div id="review_2347861503" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2347861503" />
    <a title="Lady Clementina ffinch-ffarowmore" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/5917681-lady-clementina-ffinch-ffarowmore"><img alt="Lady Clementina ffinch-ffarowmore" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1560079929p2/5917681.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2347861503?book_show_action=true">May 21, 2018</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Lady Clementina ffinch-ffarowmore" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Lady Clementina ffinch-ffarowmore" href="/user/show/5917681-lady-clementina-ffinch-ffarowmore">Lady Clementina ffinch-ffarowmore</a>
      </span>

          added it


          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback 9781782690269" href="/book/show/21028440-the-letter-for-the-king">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5917681-lady-clementina-ffinch-ffarowmore?shelf=young-adult">young-adult</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5917681-lady-clementina-ffinch-ffarowmore?shelf=english-translation">english-translation</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5917681-lady-clementina-ffinch-ffarowmore?shelf=children-s-literature">children-s-literature</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5917681-lady-clementina-ffinch-ffarowmore?shelf=adventure">adventure</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5917681-lady-clementina-ffinch-ffarowmore?shelf=tonke-dragt">tonke-dragt</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5917681-lady-clementina-ffinch-ffarowmore?shelf=knights">knights</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2347861503" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer3796206491041541997">I first heard about <i>The Letter for the King</i> when I happened to watch bits of the film version (Dutch with subtitles) on TV some time ago, and when I noticed the book on NetGalley, of course I couldn’t resist putting in a request. My thanks to Pushkin Children’s Books and NetGalley for a review copy of this title. This was written by Dragt in 1962 and the translation I read is by Laura Wilkinson, published by Pushkin Children’s Books which according to the blurb at the back of the book brings out</span>
  <span id="freeText3796206491041541997" style="display:none">I first heard about <i>The Letter for the King</i> when I happened to watch bits of the film version (Dutch with subtitles) on TV some time ago, and when I noticed the book on NetGalley, of course I couldn’t resist putting in a request. My thanks to Pushkin Children’s Books and NetGalley for a review copy of this title. This was written by Dragt in 1962 and the translation I read is by Laura Wilkinson, published by Pushkin Children’s Books which according to the blurb at the back of the book brings out children’s books old and new, from different languages and cultures. <br /><br />This was a lot like the book I last read (<i>Band of Soldiers</i>―teen heroes in times past, thrown into adventure and danger) but still a very different story, and of course in a very different place. Of course, this was part of my theme reads this month, the Kings here being the fictional kings of Dragonaut and Unawen. Sixteen-year-old Tiuri with five other, slightly ‘older’ young men are about to be knighted by their King, the King of Dragonaut. The rules of the kingdom require that they spend the night before the ceremony locked up, in quiet contemplation, without food, water, or talk, and without letting anyone in or themselves out. But when a stranger knocks at the window seeking help, Tiuri breaks these rules not only opening the window but going out to the stranger’s aid. At first his task seems simple, to deliver a letter of importance to the stranger’s master, the Black Knight with the White shield, which Tiuri thinks he can complete and be back before the ceremony, though there will be some explaining to do. But when he finds the Black Knight with the White shield has been tricked and murdered, and the Knight, before dying hands over his task to Tiuri to complete, he realises what he must do will neither be quick nor simple. He must travel all the way to the kingdom of Unawen to deliver the secret message to the King himself. Not only is the journey hard enough in itself, in pursuit of Tiuri are the Red Riders, responsible for murdering the Black Knight with the White shield, and also the Grey Knights who suspect Tiuri of the foul deed. Along the way, however, some misunderstandings clear up and he meets various people, in the forest and the cities he visits, who are more than willing to help him accomplish his task even if he can’t tell them what it is. But there are also dangers aplenty, and traps as many along the way, and Tiuri must avoid falling into these traps or being defeated (or indeed dissuaded) by the dangers if he wants to keep his word to the Knight and complete this task.<br /><br />At a little under 500 pages, this is not a short read but one which was very enjoyable for me. It may not feel as fast paced as one would expect from an adventure story but keeps one interested throughout, for while one might well know that Tiuri will accomplish his task at the end, one does want to know how he does it, and what each adventure he falls into along the way holds for him. Tiuri is a likeable character, believable as a young lad out on an adventure, doing what his heart tells him, yet regretting the Knighthood that he has lost and may never get again, and the same can be said about his friend Piak, who also finds himself at one point having to decide between two things he seems to want equally. While we may not face those very same questions, the kind of decisions they are faced with and must take, and the lessons they learn along the way are relevant for everyone in whatever age and situation. (In fact there is quite a bit of wisdom hidden in there―no not the preachy kind). ‘Villains’ seem to lurk around every corner to bring young Tiuri down but they too are not all of the same shade, as one will see, and some can surprise one. The menacing ‘main’ villain of the piece though is only one shade and very well done. Tiuri may not have been made a knight at the start of his adventure, but his courage, loyalty, and even tenacity show that he is one even if he doesn’t have the title. I enjoyed the world of knights and kings that this book took me into (and incidentally, now I finally properly understand what a Knight errant is―no I wasn’t entirely clear so far). This was also one of the few books I’ve read (there must have been others, though honestly I can’t think of one at the moment) where the return journey (though obviously shorter than the adventure itself) is given some space and doesn’t pass by in a blur. In it, old friends are met again, some explanations given, and some promise of ‘romance’ (like in the <i>Band of Soldiers</i>) is seen. I also liked the artwork, which decorates the pages between ‘parts’ of the book, very much. This is a combination of shadows/silhouettes and something like the spray feature on paintbrush (sorry again for my terrible terminology describing this) but I liked the effect the artist achieved―oh I just looked and the illustrations are by Dragt herself, something I hadn’t noticed at the beginning. Dragt, incidentally, as Wikipedia tells me, is considered “the greatest Dutch female writer for children”. I look forward to reading more of Dragt’s books and also exploring Pushkin’s other titles. Four and a half stars.</span>
  <a data-text-id="3796206491041541997" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_2914762685" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2914762685" />
    <a title="Abigail" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/87835420-abigail"><img alt="Abigail" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1539121384p2/87835420.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2914762685?book_show_action=true">Jul 28, 2019</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Abigail" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Abigail" href="/user/show/87835420-abigail">Abigail</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback 9781782690818" href="/book/show/23633448-the-letter-for-the-king">review of another edition</a>

          <div><span class="uitext greyText">Recommends it for: </span>
           <span class="uitext reviewText">Readers Who Enjoy Rollicking Good Adventure Stories</span></div>

        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/87835420-abigail?shelf=dutch-children">dutch-children</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/87835420-abigail?shelf=childrens-fiction">childrens-fiction</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/87835420-abigail?shelf=knights">knights</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/87835420-abigail?shelf=childrens-translations">childrens-translations</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/87835420-abigail?shelf=childrens-fantasy">childrens-fantasy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/87835420-abigail?shelf=pushkin-childrens-books">pushkin-childrens-books</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/87835420-abigail?shelf=ruritanian-romance">ruritanian-romance</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2914762685" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer7700469946595441237">On the eve of being knighted by his king, sixteen-year-old Tiuri, son of Tiuri the Valiant, is keeping vigil in a small chapel outside of the capital city of the kingdom of Dagonaut. Forbidden from speaking, or opening the chapel doors to anyone during his night-long fast, Tiuri does both when a mysterious old man comes begging for help. A knight in spirit, even if he is not one in fact, Tiuri is helpless to resist this supplicant in need, and soon finds himself caught up in an epic adventure in</span>
  <span id="freeText7700469946595441237" style="display:none">On the eve of being knighted by his king, sixteen-year-old Tiuri, son of Tiuri the Valiant, is keeping vigil in a small chapel outside of the capital city of the kingdom of Dagonaut. Forbidden from speaking, or opening the chapel doors to anyone during his night-long fast, Tiuri does both when a mysterious old man comes begging for help. A knight in spirit, even if he is not one in fact, Tiuri is helpless to resist this supplicant in need, and soon finds himself caught up in an epic adventure involving a slain knight, a mysterious letter that must be delivered to the king of Unauwen - the land on the far side of the Great Mountains - and a dangerous month-long journey through dark forests, across high mountains and over treacherous rivers. Determined to keep his word and fulfill his mission, Tiuri encounters many enemies on his quest, but makes many friends as well...<br /><br />Originally published in Dutch as <u>De brief voor de koning</u>, this intensely engrossing, utterly engaging children's fantasy is a delight to read. I devoured it, racing through its 500+ pages, and finishing it with an immediate desire to know more of Tiuri's adventures, by tracking down the sequel (thus far only available in English in the UK), <u>
  <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/26025311.The_Secrets_of_the_Wild_Wood" title="The Secrets of the Wild Wood by Tonke Dragt" rel="nofollow noopener">The Secrets of the Wild Wood</a>
</u>. I may have to order it from abroad... Tiuri is an appealing hero, goodhearted, rather innocent, and so determined to keep his word and to remain faithful to his principles as a knight. It is these very qualities which aid him on his journey, as his kindness and innocence win him allies, and his bravery in aiding others converts would-be enemies. This last, as exemplified through the story of Jaro, is particularly powerful. Although most online reviewers seem to love <u>The Letter for the King</u>, I have seen one or two who have criticized it for its simplicity. This, for me, is its strength and power. At its heart, this is the story about the letter of the law versus its spirit; about holding onto principles (knightly, in this case) even when it seems that the 'reward' we have expected for doing so disappears; about keeping faith and remaining true to our purpose, even in the face of danger. Simple? Yes, I suppose so - but what a rich simplicity such stories bring to us, their readers! Recommended to anyone who enjoys rollicking good adventure stories.</span>
  <a data-text-id="7700469946595441237" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_2825193375" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2825193375" />
    <a title="Eustacia Tan" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/6609117-eustacia-tan"><img alt="Eustacia Tan" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1553435967p2/6609117.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2825193375?book_show_action=true">May 18, 2019</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Eustacia Tan" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Eustacia Tan" href="/user/show/6609117-eustacia-tan">Eustacia Tan</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Hardcover 9781782690108" href="/book/show/18113445-the-letter-for-the-king">review of another edition</a>


        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2825193375" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer4061474953716668912">I heard about this book from Krysta at Pages Unbound and it sounded really interesting so I hunted down the nearest library copy. As expected, I was not disappointed.<br/><br/>The Letter Tor The King starts with Tiuri keeping vigil. This is the last task that he has to do before he becomes a knight. But when someone knocks at the door asking for help, Tiuri knows that the knightly thing to do is to help. Even if it means giving up his knighthood. And so, Tiuri starts a quest to deliver an important letter</span>
  <span id="freeText4061474953716668912" style="display:none">I heard about this book from Krysta at Pages Unbound and it sounded really interesting so I hunted down the nearest library copy. As expected, I was not disappointed.<br /><br />The Letter Tor The King starts with Tiuri keeping vigil. This is the last task that he has to do before he becomes a knight. But when someone knocks at the door asking for help, Tiuri knows that the knightly thing to do is to help. Even if it means giving up his knighthood. And so, Tiuri starts a quest to deliver an important letter to the king of the neighbouring kingdom, one that will bring him much danger and many friends.<br /><br />For some reason, this book reminded me of The Book of Three from The Chronicles of Prydain. While it doesn’t have as much humour as The Book of Three, it has the same classical feel. It’s a pretty straightforward quest and the emphasis is really more on Tiuri growing than it is on the plot (although Tiuri’s growth is not as obvious as Taran’s). I liked that Tiuri got to meet a lot of different people on the way. The main characters are Tiuri and Piak, his companion, but there was a steady amount of characters that they get to meet. I feel that having two main characters help in allowing the minor characters to have an adequate amount of page-time without it being too overwhelming.<br /><br />Although the plot wasn’t the most fast-paced, I enjoyed it. There was the right amount of mystery that made me want to read on and I was pretty satisfied by the ending as well. This isn’t like most YA fantasies that have battle after battle, but is more like The Book of Three and Lord of The Rings, which for the most part aren’t the fastest paced books.<br /><br />The Letter For The King is a classic fantasy YA that will probably appeal to fans of books like the Chronicles of Prydain. It feels like it’s aimed towards a slightly younger audience than the Chronicles of Prydain and the Hobbit, but I still really enjoyed it. I realised at the end that there are other books in the series, which I’ll have to read too.<br /><br />This review was first posted at <a href="https://eustaciatan.com/2019/05/the-letter-for-the-king-by-tonke-dragt.html" rel="nofollow noopener">Eustea Reads</a></span>

<span id="freeTextContainer10778119076015883722">This was a bit of a sad experience because <i>The Letter for the King</i> was one of my favourite books as a child, but I could tell during my reread that I wouldn't have been/wasn't as into it as an adult. I actually think this might be the rare case where I prefer the Dutch version. Part of that is definitely nostalgia-motivated, and it's not so much that you can tell this is an English translation as that it just reads very formal and literal in English, which I think might be less the case in the D</span>
  <span id="freeText10778119076015883722" style="display:none">This was a bit of a sad experience because <i>The Letter for the King</i> was one of my favourite books as a child, but I could tell during my reread that I wouldn't have been/wasn't as into it as an adult. I actually think this might be the rare case where I prefer the Dutch version. Part of that is definitely nostalgia-motivated, and it's not so much that you can tell this is an English translation as that it just reads very formal and literal in English, which I think might be less the case in the Dutch original. That being said, Tiuri and Lavinia are still OTP (and should really consider making that an OT3 with Piak) and the sequel was always my favourite of the series anyway, so maybe that one will go over better. </span>

<div id="review_2368317689" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2368317689" />
    <a title="Alyson Stone" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/33568588-alyson-stone"><img alt="Alyson Stone" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1496937455p2/33568588.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2368317689?book_show_action=true">Apr 26, 2018</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Alyson Stone" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Alyson Stone" href="/user/show/33568588-alyson-stone">Alyson Stone</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback 9781782690269" href="/book/show/21028440-the-letter-for-the-king">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/33568588-alyson-stone?shelf=arc">arc</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/33568588-alyson-stone?shelf=fantasy">fantasy</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2368317689" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer7132975680313288281">Book: The Letter for the King<br/>Author: Tonke Dragt <br/>Rating: 4 Out of 5 Stars<br/><br/>I would like to thank the publisher and Netgalley for providing me with this ARC. Well, I guess it’s not really an ARC since the book was published a long time ago, but this is a new edition. <br/><br/>So, I have never heard of this book until now. I don’t know how it could have slipped by me, but it did. The Letter for the King has everything that a great fantasy needs. It has adventure, excitement, and well written characters. It i</span>
  <span id="freeText7132975680313288281" style="display:none">Book: The Letter for the King<br />Author: Tonke Dragt <br />Rating: 4 Out of 5 Stars<br /><br />I would like to thank the publisher and Netgalley for providing me with this ARC. Well, I guess it’s not really an ARC since the book was published a long time ago, but this is a new edition. <br /><br />So, I have never heard of this book until now. I don’t know how it could have slipped by me, but it did. The Letter for the King has everything that a great fantasy needs. It has adventure, excitement, and well written characters. It is written in a more traditional, classical fantasy style. Think Lord of the Rings here people. <br /><br />The writing is amazing. Although, there were a few times that I found myself wincing. Like the Lord of the Rings, Dragt does tend to tell us what is going on instead of actually showing us in a few places. This is always a big issue for me, because whenever I am being told what is going on, it kind of feels like they are either trying to cut corners or the publisher is making them cut their book down. I don’t know which one it is. <br /><br />The characters were well developed and well written. There is a lot of them, but I didn’t have any trouble keeping them straight. It felt like that none of them were trying to get their chance in the spotlight and everyone was important. There are a lot of books that I read that just add characters for the sake of having a large cast and this is not the case here. <br /><br />This really is one of the most underrated and overlooked books that I have read in a long time. People really do need to find this book and pick it up for themselves. I think they really will be in for a surprise. <br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="7132975680313288281" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

  <span id="freeText3122302729027223950" style="display:none">Tiuri is called out of his pre-knightly vigil to help a man desperate for assistance, and, ruining his chances to become a knight, he sets off to aid the man by taking an important letter to the king.<br /><br />It's a perilous trip across the Great Mountains, and Tiuri is pursued by wicked men determined to prevent the delivery of the letter. <br /><br />It was seeing the strong character of this sixteen-year-old that I loved most about this book. Again and again, Tiuri was tested and set upon and tried and yet he always attempted to do the right thing even when he was up against truly devious men. <br /><br />This book is on the list of the 1001 Children's Books You Must Read. The author is a Dutch author and the book has won many awards and has been translated into sixteen languages. </span>

  <span id="freeText877782204127234561" style="display:none">DNF @10%<br />I wanted to read the book before Netflix adaptation came out. But just don’t feel like continuing. Nothing is wrong with this book as such. This is a middle grade book so the plot isn’t very complex. I will keep this on my shelf and give it to my son when he can read. The plot is very simple - it’s like someone made a book out of Frodo’s flight in Lord of the rings from Bagend. It’s almost like first half of the Fellowship of the ring, except that the protagonist is traveling alone with a letter AND a ring, instead of just a ring and there are riders on horses chasing him. It got tiresome after reading it for a while.</span>

              <span id="reviewTextContainer2357988067" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer11632376972398434549">When my friend and book blogger posted this glowing review of Tonke Dragt’s “The Letter for the King” last year, I was intrigued because it appeared to be all about knights and chivalry and adventure. Who doesn’t like the sound of that? A month or so ago, I found this book waiting to be reviewed on NetGalley, and my heart leapt! Thanks to Pushkin Press and NetGalley, I got a copy, and I finished reading it yesterday. <br/><br/><i>The Letter for the King is the thrilling story of one boy’s battle against evil</i></span>
  <span id="freeText11632376972398434549" style="display:none">When my friend and book blogger posted this glowing review of Tonke Dragt’s “The Letter for the King” last year, I was intrigued because it appeared to be all about knights and chivalry and adventure. Who doesn’t like the sound of that? A month or so ago, I found this book waiting to be reviewed on NetGalley, and my heart leapt! Thanks to Pushkin Press and NetGalley, I got a copy, and I finished reading it yesterday. <br /><br /><i>The Letter for the King is the thrilling story of one boy’s battle against evil, set in an enchanted <br />world of chivalry, courage and true friendship.</i><br /><br />Says the book summary from Pushkin Press. I would say, thrilling is an understatement. As soon as I reached the last page, I was Googling to see if there is any way I could procure the sequel, “The Secrets of the Wild Wood.” I couldn’t wait to go on an adventure with Tiuri again.<br /><br />The Letter for the King reinforces classic values like bravery, loyalty, and chivalry throughout Tiuri’s journey. But what makes the book rise above an average boy’s adventure is the fact that Tiuri is flawed despite having so many good qualities. He is impulsive, his bravery sometimes borders on foolhardiness, and his good heart sometimes comes in the way of his progress. <br /><br />In most cases, though, Tiuri’s sensibilities save him from slippery situations. In fact, that’s the other aspect of the book. You would think that a story about knights set in the Middle Ages would have tons of action with swords and blood and gore. The Letter for the King barely has any swordfights and, in fact, hardly any skirmishes. <br /><br />The entire book moves forward on the themes of intrigue, plotting, and little pockets of suspense. Every few pages, Tiuri comes up against an obstacle, and his fate hangs in balance for a while before it’s resolved lending the book a fairly predictable cadence. At times, due to this, it reads more like the tale of a solo traveller on a hike across the Camino rather than an action packed tale. <br /><br />Friendship is another strong theme in the book. Apart from Tiuri’s steadfast friendship with Piak, the quick bonds formed with the various people he meets on his journey, and the strong brotherhood that the knights share are all admirably and beautifully played out. But in that sense, it’s one of those books that you would stereotypically first think of for boys rather than for girls with its lack of any other emotion and significant women characters.<br /><br />Mostly, the principles in the story never go to the grey area, and there is not much ambiguity. People are either good or bad, Tiuri has either friends or enemies, and they all mostly stay that way. <br /><br />Written in the traditional manner of a good, old-fashioned adventure, the tale of Tiuri the knight has long served as one of the most loved bedtime stories for children, and a popular fantasy among adults in The Netherlands. It has been frequently compared to The Lord of the Rings where we have Frodo going on a mission, very similar to Tiuri. But I think the canvas of Tolkiens’ epic is way larger, more complex, and much darker. <br /><br />At over 500 pages long, this is one long adventure. But I never the felt the weight of time even for a second as Tiuri’s encounters kept me enthralled.</span>
  <a data-text-id="11632376972398434549" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/3263772525?book_show_action=true">Apr 25, 2020</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Blue" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Blue" href="/user/show/70806132-blue">Blue</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="paperback 9781782692591" href="/book/show/52644545-the-letter-for-the-king">review of another edition</a>


        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer3263772525" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer12057144610265804478">Want to see more...<br/><a href='http://www.instagram.com/bluefairytales_' rel='nofollow noopener'> Bookstagram</a><br/><br/><a href='http://www.bluefairytales.com.au' rel='nofollow noopener'> Website</a><br/><b> Thank you Allen & Unwin for this book in exchange for an honest review</b><br/><br/>I am actually surprised that I haven’t heard of this book before considering it has been around for a while and there is a Netflix TV show for it, guess I have been living under a rock!!<br/>I do love finding an inspiring character. Generally the hero of the story who is depicted as brave really isn’t and relies on other’s to assist them or they seem absolutely perfect and everything magicall</span>
  <span id="freeText12057144610265804478" style="display:none">Want to see more...<br /><a href="http://www.instagram.com/bluefairytales_" rel="nofollow noopener"> Bookstagram</a><br /><br /><a href="http://www.bluefairytales.com.au" rel="nofollow noopener"> Website</a><br /><b> Thank you Allen &amp; Unwin for this book in exchange for an honest review</b><br /><br />I am actually surprised that I haven’t heard of this book before considering it has been around for a while and there is a Netflix TV show for it, guess I have been living under a rock!!<br />I do love finding an inspiring character. Generally the hero of the story who is depicted as brave really isn’t and relies on other’s to assist them or they seem absolutely perfect and everything magically goes their way. Tiuri isn’t like that at all and is generally a good and kind human that honestly tries to carry out his tasks no matter what gets thrown in his path. <br />You read about a young 11 year old boy that braves the elements, the outside world and his fear as he carries on the task he know has to be done, the fate of the world rests in his hands. <br /><br />This book was soo beautiful and one of those books that I think will be an instant classic and will never age. The story was extremely well written, providing enough detail of the world building to allow you to imagine it and draws you into the story, the world and fall for the characters easily. There is well and truly enough action and adventure to keep you entertained and suitable for all ages. You also get to see the internal battle that rages on in Tiuri, were he must strive not to give up and continue on his journey no matter how hard it is. <br />I have to admit, my favourite part about this book, is it isn’t a fantasy just for adults. Considering it’s age, this book is prime for the younger audience and give them the chance to enjoy fantasy. Going back to my childhood, there really wasn’t fantasy books that I could love and enjoy, you went from Deltora Quest to Wizards First Rule, and there was no middle ground. The Letter to the King, is great for the younger generation who devour fantasy and what nothing more to emerge themselves into a fictional world that isn’t for a child nor adult. Really for a book written in 1962, this book was well before it’s time and before the literary world evolved to cover all areas of genres for all ages. This really is a book ahead of its time and I highly recommend that you read it and hope you love it as much as I did.<br /></span>

<div id="review_3353631914" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/3353631914" />
    <a title="Fiona" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/90765599-fiona"><img alt="Fiona" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1546469395p2/90765599.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/3353631914?book_show_action=true">May 26, 2020</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Fiona" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Fiona" href="/user/show/90765599-fiona">Fiona</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer3353631914" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer12262101721357210621">First published in 1962 in the Netherlands(which is where I live), this children’s book has been read by many Dutch children and adults.<br/><br/>Now, when I was younger my sister actually had a copy of this book, which was the one I was reading in for the last few days. But it never appealed to me as a child. The cover did not, the title did not and I don’t think I have ever read the synopsis. Now that I am older and the Netflix series came out, I realised this children’s literature has been a big part i</span>
  <span id="freeText12262101721357210621" style="display:none">First published in 1962 in the Netherlands(which is where I live), this children’s book has been read by many Dutch children and adults.<br /><br />Now, when I was younger my sister actually had a copy of this book, which was the one I was reading in for the last few days. But it never appealed to me as a child. The cover did not, the title did not and I don’t think I have ever read the synopsis. Now that I am older and the Netflix series came out, I realised this children’s literature has been a big part in our reading history and I should read it at least once. So I did. <br /><br />This entire book I had to keep in mind that this is a children’s book. And sometimes, those appeal less to adults. <br /><br />Tiuri is about to become a knight when a stranger calls for help. Answering to his plea, Tiuri has to deliver a letter to the king of the kingdom next to his. A very important letter. During his quest, he encounters dangerous moments, enemies and makes new friends. <br /><br />So I read this in a few days. The writing style isn’t difficult. Which is understandable since this is a children’s book. The pace is good and the story is quite nice! I love the drawn map in front, because that way I could really follow where Tiuri’s quest was taking him. I definitely understand why this is so popular under children and adults. What I am missing in this story is actual thrill and sometimes the characters are missing dept. But considering this is a children’s book and it has to keep their attention without frightening them into not being able to sleep at night, I understand. I do like how the deep friendship between Tiuri and Piak unfolds. I love how they appreciate the sights and nature around them. <br /><br />I don’t really understand why there is magic in the TV series, when there is literally non in the book. I think it is a shame actually, because that is part of the charm of this book. Magic isn’t always necessary to make a children’s or YA book great. I actually think it is really refreshing that there is no magic in it. <br /><br />This really is a classic children’s book that deserved the awards it got. As an adult now, I probably won’t read it again anytime soon. But had I read it as a kid, I probably would have reread it a dozen times. I really enjoyed reading this book and I am about to start in part two, so I would definitely recommend it!</span>
  <a data-text-id="12262101721357210621" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_3248722048" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/3248722048" />
    <a title="Smitha Murthy" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/3547543-smitha-murthy"><img alt="Smitha Murthy" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1585489620p2/3547543.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/3248722048?book_show_action=true">Mar 26, 2020</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Smitha Murthy" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Smitha Murthy" href="/user/show/3547543-smitha-murthy">Smitha Murthy</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer3248722048" class="readable"

<span id="freeTextContainer12976419932181428320">I had heard my friend rave about this book for nearly a year now. It had been quite an expensive buy, so I had put it off, until a sudden discount made me take the plunge. And now I am glad I did! In times like these, I needed a book that would just be a rollicking adventure, a travel tale that twists and slides, and at heart, a beautiful story. Who wouldn’t love that?<br/><br/>At times, I wished that I could give poor Tiuri a smartphone. All that the poor lad had to do was take a message to the King! Her</span>
  <span id="freeText12976419932181428320" style="display:none">I had heard my friend rave about this book for nearly a year now. It had been quite an expensive buy, so I had put it off, until a sudden discount made me take the plunge. And now I am glad I did! In times like these, I needed a book that would just be a rollicking adventure, a travel tale that twists and slides, and at heart, a beautiful story. Who wouldn’t love that?<br /><br />At times, I wished that I could give poor Tiuri a smartphone. All that the poor lad had to do was take a message to the King! Here, Tiuri. Take my phone. WhatsApp the King right now! But then, we wouldn’t have such a story then, would we? Perhaps, the most heartwarming part of this is the friendship between Piak and Tiuri. In Piak, Tonke Dragt has created one of the cutest characters ever. <br /><br />If you are wondering about a book to just get lost in now and forget the mad world outside, then this is the book for you. Trust me on this. I now wish I could order the sequel, but I have to wait until the world deems that books are “essential” items for delivery too. <br /></span>
